  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_265f563b-e4c8-4a81-ad61-89db0e3c9720'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer3628008004821923835"><b>CLORAL</b><br/><br/>FOURTEEN-YEAR-OLD Bobby Pendragon is not like other boys his age. His uncle Press is a Traveler, and, as Bobby has learned, that means Uncle Press is responsible, through his journeys, for solving interdimensional conflict wherever he encounters it. His mission is nothing less than to save the universe from ultimate evil. And he's taking Bobby along for the ride.<br/><br/>Fres</span>
  <span id="freeText3628008004821923835" style="display:none"><b>CLORAL</b><br /><br />FOURTEEN-YEAR-OLD Bobby Pendragon is not like other boys his age. His uncle Press is a Traveler, and, as Bobby has learned, that means Uncle Press is responsible, through his journeys, for solving interdimensional conflict wherever he encounters it. His mission is nothing less than to save the universe from ultimate evil. And he's taking Bobby along for the ride.<br /><br />Fresh from his first adventure on Denduron, Bobby finds himself in the territory of Cloral, a vast world that is entirely covered by water. Cloral is nearing a disaster of huge proportions. Reading the journals Bobby sends home, his friends learn that the desperate citizens of the endangered floating cities are on the brink of war. Can Bobby - suburban basketball star and all-around nice guy - help rid the area of marauders, and locate the legendary lost land of Faar, which may hold the key to Cloral's survival?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3628008004821923835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText16363032050287108191" style="display:none">The Lost City of Faar (Pendragon, #2), D.J. MacHale<br />The Lost City of Faar is the second book in the Pendragon series by D. J. MacHale. The people live on immense, floating cities called Habitats and grow food on the sea floor and in their habitats. Different habitats do different things such as producing food, making products, etc. It's an idyllic world until Saint Dane unleashes a poison that makes the crops grow large but fatal. To save the territory, Bobby battles pirates on the surface and killer sharks below, all in hopes of finding salvation on a legendary underwater city called Faar.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیستم ماه ژانویه سال 2010 میلادی<br />عنوان: پندراگن کتاب دوم: فار، شهر گمشده؛ نویسنده: دی.جی. مک هیل؛ مترجم: ویدا اسلامیه؛ تهران، تندیس، 1387؛ در 515 ص؛ شابک: 9789648944501؛ چاپ سوم 1392؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21 م<br />این کتاب، دومین جلد، از سری روز نگاشته های بابی پندراگن، چهارده ساله است، که به همراه دایی «پرس»، به دنیاها، و زمانهای ناشناخته، سفر میکند، تا دنیا را نجات دهد، اینبار یادداشتها، در کره ی پهناوری به نام: «کلرال»، که سراسر آن را آب فراگرفته، نگاشته میشوند، تا به دست دوستان زمینی بابی برسند. بابی، به دنبال سرزمین افسانه ای گمشده ی فار، میگردد. که احتمالا یافتنش، تنها راه نجات کلرال، و مردمش است. این دنیای خیال انگیز را چقدر دوست میدارم، منظورم این کتاب نیست، هر کتاب فانتزی مرا میرباید. ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12703179268162651393">Reread this for nostalgia's sake. 3 observations:<br/>1. Bobby Pendragon has a huge crush on Spader and you can't convince me otherwise.<br/>2. The story is still compelling as hell, but the narration issues ignored by my middle-school self now leave something to be desired.<br/>3. That being said, the plotting is MASTERFUL. It's worth sticking with a series reread just to watch it all unfold again.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2705819313?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Cyanide Latte~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Cyanide Latte~" href="/user/show/70514160-cyanide-latte">~Cyanide Latte~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/11914313-the-lost-city-of-faar">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">middle-grade sci-fi fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70514160-cyanide-latte?shelf=booktube-did-this-to-me">booktube-did-this-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70514160-cyanide-latte?shelf=pendragon-series">pendragon-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2705819313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13304503621920653748">As with the first book in this series and several other books in my shelves, I actually read this one once before, in my late middle school or early high school years, and while I didn't remember much about the first one or cared much for it in my re-read, I was definitely excited to read this one again. I remembered <i>The Lost City of Faar</i> much better than I did <i>The Merchant of Death</i>, and it still is a really good read as far as even a basic science-fiction story goes.<br/><br/>We open back onto the story </span>
  <span id="freeText13304503621920653748" style="display:none">As with the first book in this series and several other books in my shelves, I actually read this one once before, in my late middle school or early high school years, and while I didn't remember much about the first one or cared much for it in my re-read, I was definitely excited to read this one again. I remembered <i>The Lost City of Faar</i> much better than I did <i>The Merchant of Death</i>, and it still is a really good read as far as even a basic science-fiction story goes.<br /><br />We open back onto the story of Bobby's travels as his uncle takes him along to a territory called "Cloral", where the world is entirely covered in water and the people there have adapted to an aquatic lifestyle and the challenges it presents. When disaster strikes, Bobby, Uncle Press, and new friend Vo Spader are forced to find the lost city of Faar, which is a pretty stark parallel to the legends of Atlantis, in order to search for a solution to the issue. On the other side of the story, we follow along as Mark gets discovered with Bobby's journals by his tormentor from school, Andy Mitchell. Andy winds up hatching a scheme to steal all of Bobby's journals from Mark and turn them into the police for the sake of a $25k reward for having info on what happened to the Pendragon family, and Mark must swallow his pride and confess his mistake to Courtney in order to remedy the disaster.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the world-building in this particular book, and I think it's currently my favorite setting in the series. (Granted, I still have to get through the rest of the series, but that's besides the point.) The characterization and development has also improved in this particular book, though I still can't say that I'm always the fondest of Bobby himself. While he's not overtly cocky or full of himself, he does have a tendency to be very self-assured in his beliefs and opinions to the point that it can be detrimental to him. On the other hand, it was nice to get introduced to Spader, and to see Mark and Courtney's development as well. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Uncle Press dies at the end of this book, and I feel like that had initially left me wavering anyway, the first time I read it. Follow that up to the fact the next book deals with time travel and time travel always tends to be messy in narrative, and I'm not surprised that I put down the third book without finishing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Regardless, I'm happy I was able to revisit this book, and I am definitely interested to keep going with the series despite any misgivings I may have about our main character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13304503621920653748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_439413120" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/439413120" />
    <a title="Doris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2203514-doris"><img alt="Doris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239245558p2/2203514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/439413120?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doris" href="/user/show/2203514-doris">Doris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">children, teens, fans of Charlie Bone and Harry Potter</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2203514-doris?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer439413120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12275448844018356286"><br/>Pendragon on his second adventure is still an oddity. He has been trained from early childhood to be a Traveler, hopping between worlds via a gate similar to the Stargate familiar to television viewers. Now, he has reached the ripe old age of 14, and is being thrust into the role without being fully ready. <br/><br/>In the first adventure, he was about 14 and a half, and this adventure picks up shortly after. He is traveling to a water world this time, and finds it to be nearly a paradise. The description</span>
  <span id="freeText12275448844018356286" style="display:none"><br />Pendragon on his second adventure is still an oddity. He has been trained from early childhood to be a Traveler, hopping between worlds via a gate similar to the Stargate familiar to television viewers. Now, he has reached the ripe old age of 14, and is being thrust into the role without being fully ready. <br /><br />In the first adventure, he was about 14 and a half, and this adventure picks up shortly after. He is traveling to a water world this time, and finds it to be nearly a paradise. The descriptions sounded like what I have always imagined the reefs in Hawaii or Australia would be like, teeming with fish and with high visibility in the water. <br /><br />Unfortunately, there is a crises fast approaching, which necessitates the need for the Travelers to help. In this case, there are multiple Travelers – Bobby Pendragon, his Uncle Press, and their friend Spador (which I constantly keep reading as Spider). The Arch Nemesis of Travelers, Saint Dane, is after this world of Cloral, but at first the Travelers have no clue why. <br /><br />However, as the story unravels it becomes clear, and it is up to Bobby, Press, and Spador to stop Saint Dane and his minions (every evil villain needs minions, right?). Unfortunately Saint Dane is more of a minor character, a write-in if you will, than a part of the central plot.<br /><br />Throughout the story (both the first book and this one) the main issue I have is that Bobby is only 14 – yet sometimes he talks and thinks as if he is much older. At one point, he has to give a speech, off the cuff, with virtually no warning, yet gives a presentation which would make a professional speaker proud. Based on the lack of true character development, the speech, although heartfelt, is not believable based on previous actions. <br /><br />More character development is needed. All we really know about Bobby is that he played basketball, was interested in having Courtney as his girlfriend, and has done a lot of traveling. We know he misses his family but that is thrown in almost like an afterthought. <br /><br />This story could have been great if it had been more based in reality… and the final cliffhanger with the journals was well written but not logical with the actions Courtney and Mark (the recipients of Bobby's notes) had taken in the past. <br /><br />Still it’s a good story with a grand thesis. I still don't think at 14 his writing and speaking skills would be that advanced, unless Uncle Press also worked on honing those talents over the years. I will probably pick up the next book just to see where it goes. <br /><br /><br />***note to self - do not get these in CD - the whining of Bobby Pendragon is unbearable in that format and probably adversely affected my entire reaction to the series end note***<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12275448844018356286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_64393163" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64393163" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242771111p2/2299764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64393163?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64393163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1158053003266803429">Okay, it's official. I am now fully hooked on the Pendragon series.<br/><br/>Bobby Pendragon, fourteen-year-old new and confused Traveler of space and time, is headed to his next territory. This time, it's Cloral, a water territory where dry land is unheard of and the people have discovered all kinds of cool ways to use and overcome their aquatic surroundings. <br/><br/>But Cloral is also at a tipping point, thanks to the evil Traveler Saint Dane, who seems to have a diabolical plan for destroying Cloral's peace an</span>
  <span id="freeText1158053003266803429" style="display:none">Okay, it's official. I am now fully hooked on the Pendragon series.<br /><br />Bobby Pendragon, fourteen-year-old new and confused Traveler of space and time, is headed to his next territory. This time, it's Cloral, a water territory where dry land is unheard of and the people have discovered all kinds of cool ways to use and overcome their aquatic surroundings. <br /><br />But Cloral is also at a tipping point, thanks to the evil Traveler Saint Dane, who seems to have a diabolical plan for destroying Cloral's peace and prosperity. Bobby will need the help of both his mysterious but dependable Uncle Press, and the energetic and charismatic Vo Spader, who is unaware that he is actually Cloral's own Traveler. And then there's the fact that the only way to stop Saint Dane may lie with a sunken city that is hardly more than a fairy-tale...<br /><br />Cool gadgets, fun and engaging characters, and a image-rich world of water, this book is all the proof I needed that I'm going into a great series. Bobby has a fantastic first-person voice, and it's getting up there in my mind with Max and Percy Jackson from their titular series. Plus, more goes on back home on Second Earth with Mark and Courtney, and I'm looking forward to seeing them more in future novels. I am fluming full on into the next one!</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer96142861" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9228565119767156385">Pendragon: The Lost City of Farr<br/>By: DJ MacHale<br/><br/>A Book Review By: Chase Pixley<br/>	Prepare for another surprising and dramatic journey through Halla with Bobby Pendragon!<br/>	The second book in the series tells about what happens after Bobby’s win over Saint Dane on the territory of Denduron. “Malos” (AKA Saint Dane) escaped to a territory called Cloral. This oceanic territory has no land and is the home of Vo Spader, an Aquaneer (think life guard/police officer) and traveler. There is only one problem th</span>
  <span id="freeText9228565119767156385" style="display:none">Pendragon: The Lost City of Farr<br />By: DJ MacHale<br /><br />A Book Review By: Chase Pixley<br />	Prepare for another surprising and dramatic journey through Halla with Bobby Pendragon!<br />	The second book in the series tells about what happens after Bobby’s win over Saint Dane on the territory of Denduron. “Malos” (AKA Saint Dane) escaped to a territory called Cloral. This oceanic territory has no land and is the home of Vo Spader, an Aquaneer (think life guard/police officer) and traveler. There is only one problem though: Spader doesn’t know who he really is. A mysterious plague is sickening the territory’s crops and pirate-like raiders keep attacking the floating “habitats” (like a city on a barge). When Bobby and Spader are separated from Press the “Lead Traveler” must teach Spader his destiny and find the mythical island of Farr before it’s too late.<br />	This book 100% deserves 5 out of 5 stars. This tale is truly a piece of work. This page turner has an ominous storyline that makes it impossible to put down. Never underestimate this book’s thrills and chills. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7540958931672842479">I love throwback audiobooks! <br/><br/>While I wouldn't recommend this to any adults to read for the first time, if you read them back in middle school, have another quick flip through =] It's quite fun!<br/><br/>From an adult perspective, I think they're GREAT for transitioning kids to longer books. There's lots of reminders about what's been going on, and the author explains every turn of events and what different things mean in the bigger picture shortly after they happen - so I could have figured it out by then</span>
  <span id="freeText7540958931672842479" style="display:none">I love throwback audiobooks! <br /><br />While I wouldn't recommend this to any adults to read for the first time, if you read them back in middle school, have another quick flip through =] It's quite fun!<br /><br />From an adult perspective, I think they're GREAT for transitioning kids to longer books. There's lots of reminders about what's been going on, and the author explains every turn of events and what different things mean in the bigger picture shortly after they happen - so I could have figured it out by then, but a young reader who isn't used to having to make their own conclusions would have a short time to mull it over and make connections if they wanted, but would have it all explained when it became necessary. It's like training wheels!<br /><br />Example, under a spoiler cut: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Spader (totally guessing at spelling because I listened to the audiobook) returns to Faar after going to find Wu Yenza, I knew she had taken the initiative to go for help. Nothing else made sense, but I've read enough to be able to make that leap. Later, when the aquineers showed up, the characters find Wu Yenza, and she tells the story exactly as I'd expected.<br /> In an adult level novel, that wouldn't have needed to happen - anyone who didn't make the leap when she was missing would have made it when they all showed up, but it is explained very clearly.<br />  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_137011002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137011002" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4108079-k"><img alt="K" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137011002?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/4108079-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4108079-k?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer137011002&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137011002" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14655128008278404623">I liked the idea of this book a lot (even if I was disappointed with the series as a whole when I found out that Pendragon had nothing to do with King Arthur – come on!), and I would love to live on Cloral. MacHale does a pretty good job of balancing description of the world (excuse me – territory) with things actually happening, and he doesn't give us any more information than he does Bobby, which really gives the reader a chance to empathize with Bobby's confusion.<br/><br/>That said, the main story jus</span>
  <span id="freeText14655128008278404623" style="display:none">I liked the idea of this book a lot (even if I was disappointed with the series as a whole when I found out that Pendragon had nothing to do with King Arthur – come on!), and I would love to live on Cloral. MacHale does a pretty good job of balancing description of the world (excuse me – territory) with things actually happening, and he doesn't give us any more information than he does Bobby, which really gives the reader a chance to empathize with Bobby's confusion.<br /><br />That said, the main story just didn't hold my attention. It wasn't bad, necessarily, and I did enjoy it overall, but I got bored if I tried reading more than a couple of chapters at once. I thought the Mark and Courtney plot was much better done, and a lot more interesting, though I had problems with it too – see below. I think one of the reasons I got bored was that MacHale really prefers to tell than show. I can understand it; telling is easier, and I know that when I write, I have the same problem. But it does get boring to read.<br /><br />He also skips some scenes that I think really should be included, passing over them in a couple of sentences instead. I really didn't care about Spader, because almost the entire friendship between him and Bobby was reduced to a couple of pages. Bobby keeps saying how much fun they had together and how awesome Spader is, but the reader doesn't get to see that. We just see Spader being a loose cannon after his father is killed. Granted, being totally focused on vengeance in that situation is reasonable, but it's not the kind of thing that endears a character to me.<br /><br />Another thing that was skipped – and my major problem with the Mark and Courtney plotline – is the scene when Mark told Courtney about the whole problem with Andy. It was skipped to give the plotline a bit of suspense to fit with Bobby's situation. In my opinion, it comes out looking cheap and forced. It's third person limited. We're supposed to be inside Mark's head. Why was he flipping out so much about going to the police station and whether Courtney wanted to punch him if they had planned for it? This set-up works for the first read-through; on later ones, I just want to reach through the pages and shake Mark.<br /><br />Minor/borderline petty complaints: Can someone tell me if girls actually are allowed to play on the boys' team when there <i>is</i> a girls' team for the same sport? Because if it actually happens in real life, I'll withdraw my objection, but as it stands, it is uncomfortably close to the "a credit to your sex" line of thinking, and I really wish MacHale would quite mentioning it.<br /><br />And finally, every time they mention that Mark and Courtney live in Stony Brook, Conneticut, I giggle and can't take the next couple of pages seriously because the Baby-Sitters Club was from Stoneybrook, Conneticut, which is just a <i>little</i> too close for my brain.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14655128008278404623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23422601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23422601" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1202587-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291263976p2/1202587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23422601?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/1202587-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1202587-erin?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1202587-erin?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1202587-erin?shelf=read-multiple-times">read-multiple-times</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23422601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5318994763229467170">This book is the second in the series about Bobby Pendragon, who is a "Traveler" that goes to different territories (basically other worlds) and saves them from the brink of disaster. I love the sci-fi elements of the book. The Territory that Bobby travels to in this book, Cloral, is awesome. I love hearing about all the adventures Bobby goes on and the other worlds. The Bobby storylines are very engaging and exciting.<br/><br/>What REALLY drags this book down in the side storyline that takes place in Bob</span>
  <span id="freeText5318994763229467170" style="display:none">This book is the second in the series about Bobby Pendragon, who is a "Traveler" that goes to different territories (basically other worlds) and saves them from the brink of disaster. I love the sci-fi elements of the book. The Territory that Bobby travels to in this book, Cloral, is awesome. I love hearing about all the adventures Bobby goes on and the other worlds. The Bobby storylines are very engaging and exciting.<br /><br />What REALLY drags this book down in the side storyline that takes place in Bobby's "Territory" in present time. He writes down all his adventures and sends his journals to his two friends, Mark and Courtney to read. These parts are pretty excruciating to read. His friend Mark is probably the biggest pansy ever created in a story, and also a complete moron. His whole storyline revolves around a bully finding ONE PAGE of Bobby's journal, and blackmailing Mark into letting him read the rest by saying he'd go to the police with the INFORMATION he has on journals. He's doesn't even have the actual journals to show them. And Mark actually finds this threat to be terrifying? He's worried some pre-teen will go to the police with a story about magical flumes and other worlds and take him seriously? Every time we are forced to read about Mark (which I mostly skimmed the second time I read this book), we had to read paragraphs and paragraphs of him AGONIZING over what to do in this situation. If I knew that kid in real life, I'd probably always want to punch him in the face. Courtney doesn't seem to have any purpose in the book whatsoever besides being Mark's foil (and her "personality" is way over the top to show how opposite she is).<br /><br />Also: beware, the Mark/Courtney "surprise" ending is really more the author lying to you about what happened than an actual surprise.<br /><br />If you can look past the Mark/Courtney parts of this story, you will find a very enjoyable and original sci-fi/fantasy book. Continue reading this series because it only gets better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5318994763229467170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2162190740456587465" style="display:none">The Lost City of Faar picks up with Bobby's second adventure thwarting the evil Saint Dane, whose goal is to destroy all worlds and all times. This time he journeys to the water world Chloral, where he teams up with a local named Spader and his Uncle Press. Together, they must identify the turning point Saint Dane will attempt to exploit and counter his attempt to throw this world into chaos. This book is the sequil to the first Pendragon book. In this book Bobby Pendragon has traveled to a slightly futaristic world where they have learned to concentrate water into solid objects. The entire world is water terrain. He cannot travel with his friends from the previous world because the only one he made that could come could not swim.<br />In this world the man who tried to destroy the previous one was there as well engaging him in yet another battle. He makes even more friends and has a great time until the fights that are inevitable come.<br />In this book he finds a mystical underwater city that is the only land on the entire planet and learns the secrets of saving them from their underwater world and bringing them to the surface. Also he learns how they came to be underwater in the first place and why. In the end more twists and battles take place, this is a fast action book with a great plot at the same time.<br />The book is in my opinion a great story and teaches lessons like not to interfear with things that have nothing to do with you and to listen to others warnings regardless of how outrageous they may sound.</span>

<div id="review_151961205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151961205" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151961205?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cherie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cherie" href="/user/show/4972687-cherie">Cherie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151961205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15608454064790818703">Synopsis:<br/><br/>Fourteen-year-old Bobby Pendragon is not like other boys his age. His uncle Press is a Traveler, and, as Bobby has learned, that means Uncle Press is responsible, through his journeys, for solving interdimensional conflict wherever he encounters it. His mission is nothing less than to save the universe from ultimate evil. And he’s taking Bobby along for the ride.<br/>Fresh from his first adventure on Denduron, Bobby finds himself in the territory of Cloral, a vast world that is entirely cove</span>
  <span id="freeText15608454064790818703" style="display:none">Synopsis:<br /><br />Fourteen-year-old Bobby Pendragon is not like other boys his age. His uncle Press is a Traveler, and, as Bobby has learned, that means Uncle Press is responsible, through his journeys, for solving interdimensional conflict wherever he encounters it. His mission is nothing less than to save the universe from ultimate evil. And he’s taking Bobby along for the ride.<br />Fresh from his first adventure on Denduron, Bobby finds himself in the territory of Cloral, a vast world that is entirely covered by water. Cloral is nearing a disaster of huge proportions. Reading the journals Bobby sends home, his friends learn that the desperate citizens of the endangered floating cities are on the brink of war. Can Bobby – suburban basketball star and all-around nice guy – help rid the area of marauders, and locate the legendary lost land of Faar, which may hold the key to Cloral’s survival?<br /><br />My thoughts:<br /><br />I originally started reading this series to guage whether my son would like it. I thought the first book in the series was quite good and had enough excitement to keep him reading, but of course then I wanted to see where the series lead.<br /><br />The thing I notice about these books is that they are very descriptive. The author really tries to keep kids interested with a lot of colourful and exciting adjectives, fun jokes, and interesting languges, all while there is some adventure (or disaster) going on.<br /><br />If you're like me and not worried that they are for younger readers, then it's a fun quick read. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_476289286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476289286" />
    <a title="Joel N" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15401694-joel-n"><img alt="Joel N" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476289286?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joel N" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joel N" href="/user/show/15401694-joel-n">Joel N</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476289286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11833976304482866892">The Lost City of Faar is a great book. It is the second book in the Pendragon series. The main character of the story, Bobby Pendragon is a traveler travels around territories using flumes and travels to theses territories to stop the enemy, Saint Dane from causing chaos in the territory and destroying it. Bobby, and his uncle Press go to a territory called Cloral and meet up with Spader, a boy who was soon to be the next traveler of that territory, and try to find the turning point of the terri</span>
  <span id="freeText11833976304482866892" style="display:none">The Lost City of Faar is a great book. It is the second book in the Pendragon series. The main character of the story, Bobby Pendragon is a traveler travels around territories using flumes and travels to theses territories to stop the enemy, Saint Dane from causing chaos in the territory and destroying it. Bobby, and his uncle Press go to a territory called Cloral and meet up with Spader, a boy who was soon to be the next traveler of that territory, and try to find the turning point of the territory in which Saint Dane will do something and cause destruction. The author likes to switch between what Bobby writes in his journals and what his friends, Courtney and Mark think about the journals and what they do every day, in the territory of Second Earth. I think that when the author goes back to the point of view of Mark and Courtney, you tend to lose interest in them and want to go back to what Bobby write in his journals immediately. One part of the story I can relate to is when Spader becomes stubborn and doesn't listen to what Bobby or Press says and causes a tragic event to happen. The imagery in this book is shown when Bobby just enters Cloral and describes all the weird things he sees that aren't like things in Second Earth. You start to get pulled into the story when the rising action starts occurring and a lot of crazy events happen in the story. I would recommend this book to people who like adventure stories and people who enjoy reading series. It is best if you read the first book to get an idea of how things work in Bobby's life and the traveler business.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11833976304482866892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Dawson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18126722-dawson"><img alt="Dawson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/558476799?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawson" href="/user/show/18126722-dawson">Dawson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer558476799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2826299516000582746"> The Lost City of Faar is the second book in the Pendragon series. It follows Bobby Pendragon, a time traveler of the mythical universe Halla.<br/> After the events of the first book, Bobby returns home from Denduron, a world in Halla, to find his house, family, and records gone. He has no. choice but to return to Halla with his uncle Press and help another world from the clutches of the evil St. Dane, also a traveler. This time, he must go to a planet dominated by water, Cloral. Cloral's citizens li</span>
  <span id="freeText2826299516000582746" style="display:none"> The Lost City of Faar is the second book in the Pendragon series. It follows Bobby Pendragon, a time traveler of the mythical universe Halla.<br /> After the events of the first book, Bobby returns home from Denduron, a world in Halla, to find his house, family, and records gone. He has no. choice but to return to Halla with his uncle Press and help another world from the clutches of the evil St. Dane, also a traveler. This time, he must go to a planet dominated by water, Cloral. Cloral's citizens live on platforms on the water. As they land in Cloral, a shark attacks them, and a native of Cloral, Spader, rescues them.<br /> After Bobby and Press settle in Cloral, two platforms collide; Grallion, the feeder of Cloral, and Magorran, the goods-maker of Cloral. It is revealed that the people in Magorran have died by a poisonous substance, young Spader's father among them. As they discover this, Grallion is attacked by pirates.<br /> With Cloral in danger, the only way he can save it is to appeal to the ancient protectors of Cloral, the Faarians, and get them to help - it may be their last hope.<br /> This book was a very good read. It was entertaining, especially with the whole time and space travel idea. The characters have flaws, and to see them overcome them is satisfying. It will leave you hanging, but if it didn't, who would want to continue the series?<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2826299516000582746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159247205?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Johnson" href="/user/show/1813014-chris-johnson">Chris Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159247205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7571654254572294825">I really, really enjoyed this book. In many ways more so than the first. Bobby is much more mature than he is in the first adventure and he seems to have accepted that he is a Traveler and "that is the way things are meant to be." The story was very well-paced, and I was actually bummed when the writer went back to discuss how things were going on Second Earth. I will say this though...I hate Andy Mitchell. I mean truly I can't stand that annoying kid. For a writer to have me display this much e</span>
  <span id="freeText7571654254572294825" style="display:none">I really, really enjoyed this book. In many ways more so than the first. Bobby is much more mature than he is in the first adventure and he seems to have accepted that he is a Traveler and "that is the way things are meant to be." The story was very well-paced, and I was actually bummed when the writer went back to discuss how things were going on Second Earth. I will say this though...I hate Andy Mitchell. I mean truly I can't stand that annoying kid. For a writer to have me display this much emotion toward a character says quite a bit about his writing talents. The only issue I have with the books so far is that in Bobby's journals, his vocabulary is way more than advanced than any 14-year-old I've ever met. That's a minor complaint however. <br /><br />Anyway I won't drag this on. If you're reading this, you obviously read the first book and are interested in the second in the series. You will definitely enjoy it. I'm very glad that MacHale is not shy about the topic of death and he will definitely kill characters when their time is up in the series. Very, very curious as to how this series ends up. Onto book number 3.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7571654254572294825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17739867280516509659">So it was a three right up until the very end. Fantastic but annoying.<br/><br/>Bobby talks way too much. The book could be half the size if he'd just cut down on the endless commenting. I also didn't enjoy Spader that much, and I felt like Bobby was telling me to like him because of what the character was supposed to be, rather than just showing me his awesomeness. Which, he wasn't. The world is a good idea, but it wasn't, I dunno, random enough. It could've been way more out there. And the plot was pret</span>
  <span id="freeText17739867280516509659" style="display:none">So it was a three right up until the very end. Fantastic but annoying.<br /><br />Bobby talks way too much. The book could be half the size if he'd just cut down on the endless commenting. I also didn't enjoy Spader that much, and I felt like Bobby was telling me to like him because of what the character was supposed to be, rather than just showing me his awesomeness. Which, he wasn't. The world is a good idea, but it wasn't, I dunno, random enough. It could've been way more out there. And the plot was pretty straightforward, no particular brilliance on either part, the goodguys or the badguys (although it got pretty tense at the end, edge of my seat literally :) ). And the way they won almost seemed to happen on accident.<br /><br />And then the last fifty or so pages just made me happy all over again. I'd forgotten about the death at the end and it made me cry! And then Loor was awesome. And then Bobby made me laugh with his new way of getting his journals to Mark and Courtney and his letter to them.<br /><br />I'm still conflicted. There are parts I really really like. And there are parts I just shake my head at. Hopefully DJM will get better.</span>

  <span id="freeText12783522906582144746" style="display:none">After Pendragon's feat on Denduron, Saint Dane travels to Cloral to attempt to destroy the territory. Bobby and his uncle follow, upon ariving they are attacked by wild sharks, and saved by a fellow traveler. His name is Spader. Spader, Press, and Pendragon set out to find out Saint Dandes plot to destroy this planet totally covered by water. They live on floating barges, the size of cities. Spader is going to another barge to reunite with his father, Pendragon and Press follow along, what they find is that the whole barge is empty. All 10,000 occupants have been killed by a poison. They trace the poison to the rice the occupants ate earlier that day, upon testing other farms in the area they can conclude that the whole planet has been infected by this poison. Food is going to become scarce and war will break out for it, destroying the territory. Can the travelers find the lost city of Faar? Believed to only be a fable, this is the last hope for the territory...</span>

<div id="review_34910558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34910558" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1606271-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241461585p2/1606271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34910558?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/1606271-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34910558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15284590302111786289">Great pre-teen to teen series. I wouldn't be surprised if the author was Mormon. It's about this kid who's Uncle is a traveler and takes him to another world to save it from the St. Dane who is hell bent on making war on each of the planets. Each book takes place on a different planet. It's very fun and entertaining. All about sticking to your values to achieve good. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_3002366'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3002366-the-travelers"><img alt="The Travelers (Pendragon: Before the War, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1348315076l/3002366._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JHYW6MgH4unrTh6JcsNPM8db427iurDQ4JUpHXr38cWGC5LTo3dIo7CRtzDRtdpw/Ldi+3U65KvemPp8CRIpCw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('taI+ELsqwa+0FZYAajfPMs3W5q1JBIdze4FUerLwD+MX37or0Fpr5e/KP7nJQVpx9jpnON6E0whFjIcbwRXXLQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2999335796820519524">D.J. MacHale is a writer, director, executive producer and creator of several popular television series and movies.<br/><br/>He was raised in Greenwich, CT and graduated from Greenwich High School.   <span id="freeText2999335796820519524" style="display:none">D.J. MacHale is a writer, director, executive producer and creator of several popular television series and movies.<br /><br />He was raised in Greenwich, CT and graduated from Greenwich High School. While in school, he had several jobs including collecting eggs at a poultry farm, engraving sports trophies and washing dishes in a steakhouse...in between playing football and running track. D.J. then attended New York University where he received a BFA in film production.<br /><br />His filmmaking career began in New York where he worked as a freelance writer/director, making corporate videos and television commercials. He also taught photography and film production.<br /><br />D.J. broke into the entertainment business by writing several ABC Afterschool Specials. After moving to Los Angeles, he made the fulltime switch from informational films, to entertainment. As co-creator of the popular Nickelodeon series: Are You Afraid of the Dark?, he produced all 91 episodes over 8 years. He wrote and directed many of the episodes including the CableAce nominated The Tale of Cutter's Treasure starring Charles S. Dutton. He was nominated for a Gemini award for directing The Tale of the Dangerous Soup starring Neve Campbell.<br /><br />D.J. also wrote and directed the movie Tower of Terror for ABC's Wonderful World of Disney which starred Kirsten Dunst and Steve Guttenberg. The Showtime series Chris Cross was co-created, written and produced by D.J. It received the CableAce award for Best Youth Series.<br /><br />D.J. co-created and produced the Discovery Kids series Flight 29 Down for which he writes all the episodes and directs several. His work on Flight 29 Down has earned him both Writers Guild of America and Directors Guild of America award nominations.<br /><br />Other notable writing credits include the classic ABC Afterschool Special titled Seasonal Differences; the pilot for the long-running PBS/CBS series Ghostwriter; and the HBO series Encyclopedia Brown, Boy Detective for which he received a CableAce nomination for writing.<br /><br />In print, D.J. has co-written the book The Tale of the Nightly Neighbors, based on his own teleplay and penned the poetic adaptation of the classic Norwegian folk tale East of the Sun and West of the Moon.<br /><br />The book series: Pendragon - Journal of an Adventure through Time and Space marks D.J.'s first turn as a novelist. He plans for this series of Young Adult adventures to span a total of 10 books.<br /><br />D.J. lives in Southern California with his wife Evangeline and daughter Keaton. They are avid backpackers, scuba divers and skiers. Rounding out the household are a Golden Retriever, Maggie; and a Kitten, Kaboodle. </span>

</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_4415692').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_4415692').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_4415692').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
